**Input:**

*Read Issue #227 body*  

```bash
gh issue view 227 --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --json body 2>/dev/null | jq -r '.body' | head -80
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 04:43:18  
## Problem  

In `types/agent.ts`, `programArgs` (line 456) and `owner` (line 186) are separate top-level fields on the Agent type. There is no association between who set the program args and what they are. This makes it unclear whether args were set by the user, by AI Maestro, or by another agent.  

## Current State  

```typescript
// types/agent.ts
programArgs?: string   // line 456
owner?: string         // line 186
```

## Proposed Fix  

Consider grouping related launch configuration into a structured object:  

```typescript
launchConfig?: {
  program: string
  args?: string
  owner?: string        // who configured this
  trustLevel?: 'full' | 'standard' | 'restricted'
}
```

This would also support Issue #223 (auto-trust mechanism) by providing a place to specify trust level during creation.  

## Source  

AIM-222 audit (10.7), verified unaddressed in v0.23.9.  

</details>

**Result:**

     1→# Per-Agent Program Arguments: Unified Storage, UI, and First-Launch Handling  
     2→  
     3→## Context  
     4→  
     5→PR #162 added the Agent CLI (`aimaestro-agent.sh`) which supports passing CLI arguments to programs via `-- <args>`. PR #163 added a `claudeArgs` field to the Agent Profile UI. However:  
     6→  
     7→1. **The CLI sends `programArgs` (array) but the API silently drops it** — field not in type definitions  
     8→2. **The UI stores `claudeArgs` (string)** — different name/format than the CLI  
     9→3. **The Wake API sends bare `"claude" Enter`** — never appends any arguments  
    10→4. **The Create Wizard doesn't collect CLI arguments**  
    11→5. **Resume flags (--continue, resume --last, --resume) must be skipped on first launch** when no prior session exists  
    12→  
    13→This PR unifies everything under `programArgs` (string) and makes the wake API actually use them.  
    14→  
    15→## Approach: Unified `programArgs` (string)  
    16→  
    17→- **Single field name**: `programArgs` on the Agent — replaces both `claudeArgs` (UI) and the CLI's array format  
    18→- **String format**: Easier to edit in UI, stored as-is, split by shell when passed to tmux  
    19→- **`launchCount`**: Integer on Agent, starts at 0, incremented on each wake — used to detect first launch  
    20→- **Resume pattern stripping**: Per-program regex map strips resume/continue flags when `launchCount === 0`  
    21→  
    22→## Files to Modify  
    23→  
    24→### 1. `types/agent.ts`  
    25→  
    26→**Rename `claudeArgs` → `programArgs`, add `launchCount`:**  
    27→  
    28→- Line 174: Change `claudeArgs?: string` to `programArgs?: string` with comment: `// CLI arguments passed to the program on launch`  
    29→- Line ~175: Add `launchCount?: number` with comment: `// Number of times agent has been woken/launched (0 = never launched)`

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:43:57]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 04:44:05]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Here's what I found. There are **two different "team" concepts** already coexisting in AI Maestro:  

### 1. `agent.team` — Simple string label (types/agent.ts:187)  
```typescript
team?: string  // Team name (e.g., "Backend Team", "23blocks")
```
This is just organizational metadata on the Agent. A flat string, no foreign key relationship.  

### 2. `Team` — Full entity for Team Meetings (types/team.ts)  
```typescript
interface Team {
  id: string              // UUID
  name: string            // "Backend Squad"
  agentIds: string[]      // Agent UUIDs
  instructions?: string   // Per-team CLAUDE.md
  // ... timestamps, meetings, tasks, documents
}
```
This is a full entity stored in `~/.aimaestro/teams/teams.json`, with its own task boards (`tasks-{teamId}.json`), documents (`docs-{teamId}.json`), and a meeting state machine (`idle → selecting → ringing → active`).  

### The conflict  

These two are **already disconnected**. `agent.team = "Backend Team"` has zero relationship to a `Team` entity with `name: "Backend Team"`. There's no lookup, no foreign key, no sync. An agent could say `team: "Backend Team"` but not be in any `Team`'s `agentIds` array, or vice versa.  

I don't have full context on what specific "rules about teams" you're referring to from a prior conversation (that context was compacted). Could you clarify what you had in mind? Specifically:  

- Were you planning to add rules/constraints to the `agent.team` string field (e.g., enforcing that it matches a `Team.name`)?  
- Or were you talking about something else entirely — like access control rules, team-level permissions, or workgroup-based routing?  

Knowing this will let me assess whether there's a real naming collision or if the two concepts can continue to coexist safely.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:18:45]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

in summary, the problem was that all agents can now freely message all other agents. but this would cause problems and chaos/errors if a group of agents is working on a common goal/repo/project and an agent not part of their team starts sending wrong messages or simply notifications to all other agents like a broadcast, because this will mess the communications pipelines between members of the same team. so to avoid making agents working on different projects/teams receiving the wrong messages about the other teams directives, it is necessary to create a rule that 2 type of teams exist: an open team, and a closed team. the open team members will be able to receive and send messages to other agents like now, but the members of the closed teams will be isolated from the agents outside their team, and will not be able to send or receive any messages except from members of their own team. This has only 2 exceptions: the team leader of each closed team, that I called CHIEF-OF-STAFF, and the global leader of all teams, called MANAGER. The Manager will be a singleton, and only one agent can be entitled with the MANAGER identity. Instead there can be an any number of agents entitled with the CHIEF-OF-STAFF identity, since every team can have its own Chief-of-staff/leader. Another issue similar is the assignement of the agents to the various teams. To avoid agents joining and leaving teams at random (and sending messages while joined, and then leaving, creating a strategy exploit to nullify the messaging team restrictions in practice) it is necessary to make only the MANAGER agent and the CHIEF-OF-STAFF agents able to assign/remove agents from the various teams, and also the only ones to be able to create or delete teams. And because these 2 figures can create teams and move people around, they are the only ones that can belong to multiple teams at the same time. for example the chief-of-staff can coordinate different teams and act as a bridge. Because of this, the Manager and the Chief-Of-Staff can belong to multiple teams and receive messages from all the agents with no filters, acting as a communication secretary for the whole team, while all the normal agents can only belong to one team at any time, and if the team is a closed team, they cannot receive or send messages to any agent except those belonging to their team. If the agents belonging to a team want to ask something to another team member, they should ask the chief-of-staff to ask for them, since only the chief-of-staff of their team can act as a communication intermediary. They cannot send messages to the Manager (unless he is part of their team), but the manager can send messages to everybody. This is the system that should implemented. To ensure security, only the user can assign the title of MANAGER or of CHIEF-OF-STAFF. non human agents can't decide them. to enforce security, a password should be created for the user, and when the user assign or remove the roles of MANAGER or of CHIEF-OF-

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:20:20]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:20:33]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. Here's my analysis:  

## The Conflict Is Real  

The existing **Team Meeting** feature and your proposed **messaging governance** have incompatible rules:  

| Property | Current Team Meeting | Proposed Messaging Teams |  
|----------|---------------------|-------------------------|  
| **Creation** | Anyone via UI | Only MANAGER / CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| **Add/remove agents** | Anyone via UI | Only MANAGER / CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| **Multi-membership** | Yes (agent in many teams) | No (normal agents: one team only) |  
| **Roles** | None | MANAGER, CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| **Messaging filter** | None | Closed teams: intra-team only |  
| **Purpose** | War room / kanban | Organizational access control |  
| **Lifecycle** | Ephemeral (meetings) | Persistent (org structure) |  

Bolting the governance rules onto the existing `Team` entity would break the Team Meeting feature — users can no longer freely create meeting rooms or add agents to multiple meetings.  

## The Enforcement Point  

The AMP route handler at `app/api/v1/route/route.ts` currently has **zero team awareness**. The filter would go between sender resolution (~line 333) and delivery (~line 569). Clean insertion point — no existing logic to untangle.  

## Three Options  

**Option A: Separate "Workgroup" entity** — New `Workgroup` type parallel to `Team`. Team Meeting untouched. Messaging filter checks workgroup membership. Downside: two concepts that sound similar ("why am I in a team AND a workgroup?").  

**Option B: Rename existing feature to "Meeting Room", repurpose "Team"** — Rename `Team` → `MeetingRoom` throughout the codebase. Then "Team" becomes the governance entity. Cleanest conceptually, but large rename across ~30 files (types, API routes, components, hooks, registries).  

**Option C: Extend Team with optional `messagingPolicy`** — Add `messagingPolicy?: { type: 'open' | 'closed', chiefOfStaffIds: string[] }` to the existing Team. Teams without a policy keep current behavior. Teams with a policy enforce restrictions. Problem: the "one team per agent" rule still conflicts with meeting multi-membership.  

My recommendation is **Option A** (Workgroup). It's the only option that:  
- Doesn't break any existing feature  
- Doesn't require a large rename  
- Keeps concepts clearly separated (meetings vs. org structure)  
- The naming confusion is manageable with good UI labels ("Meeting Rooms" vs. "Workgroups" in the sidebar)  

The user-facing confusion can be mitigated: in the UI, Team Meetings are already labeled as "meetings" with a meeting metaphor (ring, join, end). Workgroups would appear in a different section as organizational units.  

What's your preference? Or do you have a different naming idea that feels less confusing?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:25:52]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:26:31]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:26:42]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

You've identified the exact flaw in Option A. Let me reconsider.  

The existing architecture already has the right separation:  

```
Team  → owns kanban (tasks-{teamId}.json), documents, instructions
  └── Meeting → a session started with a team's members (separate entity)
```

Meetings are already decoupled from Teams (`types/team.ts:29` — `Meeting` has its own `id`, `agentIds`, `status`). The Team owns the project kanban; the Meeting is just a "war room session."  

This means we **don't need a separate Workgroup entity**. We can add governance directly to the existing Team, with a type distinction:  

## Revised Approach: Governed Teams  

Add `type: 'open' | 'closed'` to the existing `Team` interface:  

| Property | `open` Team (current behavior) | `closed` Team (new) |  
|----------|-------------------------------|---------------------|  
| **Creation** | Anyone via UI | Only MANAGER / CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| **Add/remove agents** | Anyone via UI | Only MANAGER / CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| **Multi-membership** | Yes | No (normal agents: max 1 closed team) |  
| **Messaging** | No restrictions | Intra-team only (except CHIEF-OF-STAFF) |  
| **Kanban/Tasks** | Per-team (existing) | Per-team (existing, isolated) |  
| **Meetings** | Works as today | Works as today (within the team) |  

The "one team per agent" rule applies **only to closed teams**. An agent can still be in multiple `open` teams (preserving current Meeting Room behavior). But they can be in at most **one** `closed` team.  

This means:  
- Existing Team Meeting feature: **zero breaking changes** (all current teams default to `type: 'open'`)  
- Kanban isolation: **automatic** — closed team's `tasks-{teamId}.json` is already separate  
- Messaging filter: goes into `app/api/v1/route/route.ts` before delivery  
- No new entity type, no rename, no conceptual confusion  

The only new pieces are:  
1. `type` field on Team  
2. Global `MessagingGovernance` config (MANAGER id, password hash)  
3. `chiefOfStaffId` per Team  
4. ACL check in team CRUD API routes  
5. Messaging filter in AMP route handler  

Does this approach work for you, or do you see remaining conflicts?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:33:52]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:33:58]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:34:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Those constraints fit cleanly into the design. Here's how each one maps to enforcement points:  

### 1. Assignment ACL (closed teams)  

**Where:** `app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts` — the `PATCH`/`PUT` handler that updates `agentIds`  

```
Before modifying agentIds on a closed team:
  → Check: is the requester the MANAGER or the team's CHIEF-OF-STAFF?
  → If not: reject with 403
```

Open teams: unchanged (anyone can add/remove as today).  

### 2. Forced transfer on assignment  

**Where:** Same team update handler, after ACL passes  

```
When adding agentId X to closed team B:
  → Scan all other closed teams for agentId X
  → If found in closed team A: remove X from A's agentIds, save A
  → Then add X to B's agentIds, save B
```

This is atomic — the agent never belongs to two closed teams simultaneously. No "decision" by the agent; it's an admin action by MANAGER/CHIEF-OF-STAFF.  

### 3. Kanban visibility ACL  

**Where:** `app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/route.ts` and `app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/[taskId]/route.ts`  

```
Before returning or modifying tasks for a closed team:
  → Check: is the requester a member of this team's agentIds?
  → OR: is the requester the MANAGER?
  → OR: is the requester a CHIEF-OF-STAFF of this team?
  → If none: reject with 403
```

The UI kanban board (`TaskKanbanBoard.tsx`) would also need a front-end guard — but the real enforcement is server-side in the API routes.  

### Summary of all enforcement points  

| Rule | Enforcement Location | Check |  
|------|---------------------|-------|  
| Create/delete closed team | `app/api/teams/route.ts` POST/DELETE | Requester is MANAGER or any CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| Assign/remove agents (closed) | `app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts` PATCH | Requester is MANAGER or team's CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| Forced transfer | Same as above | Auto-remove from previous closed team |  
| Kanban read/write (closed) | `app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/*` | Member OR MANAGER OR CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| Messaging filter (closed) | `app/api/v1/route/route.ts` | Sender and recipient in same closed team, OR sender/recipient is MANAGER/CHIEF-OF-STAFF |  
| Role assignment (MANAGER/COS) | New API endpoint | User password verification (bcrypt hash) |  

Is the spec complete, or are there more constraints you want to add before I file this as a GitHub issue and start planning the implementation?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:37:51]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:38:08]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:38:13]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good security consideration. A recovery channel that agents can't access — the natural option on macOS would be a **native system dialog** via `osascript`:  

```bash
osascript -e 'display dialog "Your recovery code: ABC-123-XYZ" with title "AI Maestro Password Reset"'
```

Agents in tmux sessions have no access to macOS UI elements. The recovery flow would be:  

1. User triggers password reset via the **web dashboard** (button in settings, not API)  
2. Server generates a one-time recovery code (expires in 5 minutes)  
3. Code displayed via **macOS native dialog** (not in any terminal, not in any API response)  
4. User enters the code + new password in the dashboard  
5. Old hash replaced with new hash  

Agents can't intercept any step: they don't control the browser, can't see macOS dialogs, and the code never appears in API responses or tmux output.  

I'll include this as a "Phase 2" requirement in the issue — documented but not in the initial implementation.  

Shall I file this as a GitHub issue now with the full spec and start planning the implementation?  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:43:08]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:43:26]*


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:43:35]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

You're right on all counts. Let me revise the recovery mechanism:  

### Password Recovery — Correct Design  

**Problem:** The API is agent-accessible, so the entire recovery flow must bypass the HTTP API.  

**Solution:** Server-side process generates the code and pushes it through **OS-native notifications only** — never through the API, never to a file, never to stdout/logs.  

| Platform | Notification Method | Command |  
|----------|-------------------|---------|  
| macOS | Notification Center | `osascript -e 'display notification "..." with title "..."'` |  
| Linux | Desktop notifications | `notify-send "AI Maestro" "Recovery code: ..."` (libnotify) |  
| Linux (no GUI) | Wall message | `wall "AI Maestro recovery code: ..."` (broadcasts to all TTYs) |  
| Future | Extensible | Platform detection + pluggable notifier |  

**Key constraints:**  
- Code generated **in-memory only** — never written to disk, API response, or logs  
- Code validated by a **separate internal mechanism** (not exposed as an API route) — e.g., a Unix domain socket that only the server process listens on, or a special admin CLI command that reads from stdin  
- Code expires after ~2 minutes  
- Agents in tmux sessions can't see OS desktop notifications (they only see their tmux pane)  
- `wall` on headless Linux is visible to TTYs but agents would need to be actively monitoring `/dev/pts/*` to intercept — and they'd need to know a recovery was triggered  

This isn't bulletproof (a sufficiently creative agent could try to monitor notifications), but it's a strong barrier against normal agent operations.  

I'll include this as a documented Phase 2 requirement in the issue. Shall I file the full issue now?  

</div>

     5→## Summary  
     6→  
     7→The Team Meeting system in AI Maestro is a full-featured multi-agent coordination UI with teams, meetings, tasks, documents, and a kanban board. There is **ZERO authentication or authorization** across all API routes -- this is by design (Phase 1 is localhost-only). All CRUD operations are open to any caller on localhost. Teams and tasks are stored as JSON files on disk under `~/.aimaestro/teams/`.  
     8→  
     9→---  
    10→  
    11→## 1. Team CRUD API Routes  
    12→  
    13→### `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/route.ts`  
    14→- **GET /api/teams** -- Lists all teams via `loadTeams()` from `lib/team-registry.ts`  
    15→- **POST /api/teams** -- Creates a new team  
    16→  - **Validation:** `name` required (string); `agentIds` must be array if provided  
    17→  - **No auth checks whatsoever**  
    18→  - Calls `createTeam({ name, description, agentIds })` which generates a UUID, timestamps, and persists to `~/.aimaestro/teams/teams.json`  
    19→  
    20→### `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts`  
    21→- **GET /api/teams/[id]** -- Returns single team by UUID, 404 if not found  
    22→- **PUT /api/teams/[id]** -- Updates team fields: `name`, `description`, `agentIds`, `lastMeetingAt`, `instructions`, `lastActivityAt`

     5→  
     6→The AMP (Agent Messaging Protocol) system in AI Maestro has two parallel message delivery paths:  
     7→1. **AMP v1 Route** (`/api/v1/route`) - The formal AMP protocol endpoint, used by CLI scripts and external agents. Authenticated via API keys.

## CONTEXT  

AI Maestro is a Next.js 14 dashboard for managing AI coding agents. It has a Team Meeting system where teams are groups of agents with kanban boards, tasks, and documents. Currently there is ZERO authentication/authorization on any API route (Phase 1 = localhost-only).  

The user wants to add messaging governance to prevent agents from different projects/teams from interfering with each other's communications and kanban boards.  

## REQUIREMENTS  

### Team Types  
- Add `type: 'open' | 'closed'` to existing Team entity  
- Open teams: current behavior (no restrictions, anyone can create/manage)  
- Closed teams: strict messaging isolation and access control  

### Roles  
- **MANAGER**: Global singleton. Can manage ALL teams, send/receive to ALL agents, belong to multiple teams.  
- **CHIEF-OF-STAFF**: Per-team leader. Can manage their team, send/receive to ALL age

This plan adds team governance (open/closed teams with messaging isolation) to AI Maestro. Open teams retain current behavior with zero breaking changes.

{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/v1/route/route.ts",
  "offset": 1,

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * AMP v1 Route Endpoint  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue  
    28→ */

   202→export function extractApiKeyFromHeader(authHeader: string | null): string | null {  
   203→  if (!authHeader) return null  
   204→  
   205→  if (authHeader.startsWith('Bearer ')) {  
   206→    return authHeader.substring(7)  
   207→  }  
   208→

   217→/**  
   218→ * Rotate an API key  
   219→ * Creates a new key and sets expiration on the old one  
   220→ */  
   221→export function rotateApiKey(oldApiKey: string): AMPKeyRotationResponse | null {  
   222→  const keys = loadApiKeys()  
   223→  const oldKeyHash = hashApiKey(oldApiKey)  
   224→  
   225→  const oldRecord = keys.find(k => k.key_hash === oldKeyHash && k.status === 'active')  
   226→  if (!oldRecord) {  
   227→    return null  
   228→  }  
   229→  
   230→  // Create new key  
   231→  const newApiKey = generateApiKey()  
   232→  const newKeyHash = hashApiKey(newApiKey)  
   233→  
   234→  const now = new Date()  
   235→  const graceExpiry = new Date(now.getTime() + KEY_ROTATION_GRACE_PERIOD_MS)  
   236→  
   237→  // Update old key with expiration  
   238→  oldRecord.expires_at = graceExpiry.toISOString()  
   239→  
   240→  // Create new key record  
   241→  const newRecord: AMPApiKeyRecord = {  
   242→    key_hash: newKeyHash,  
   243→    agent_id: oldRecord.agent_id,  
   244→    tenant_id: oldRecord.tenant_id,  
   245→    address: oldRecord.address,  
   246→    created_at: now.toISOString(),  
   247→    expires_at: null,  
   248→    status: 'active'  
   249→  }  
   250→  
   251→  keys.push(newRecord)  
   252→  saveApiKeys(keys)  
   253→  
   254→  console.log(`[AMP Auth] Rotated API key for agent ${oldRecord.agent_id.substring(0, 8)}...`)  
   255→  
   256→  return {  
   257→    api_key: newApiKey,  
   258→    expires_at: null,  
   259→    previous_key_valid_until: graceExpiry.toISOString()  
   260→  }

   244→    !a.deletedAt &&

   246→    a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === selfHostId  
   247→  ) || null

   215→    console.error(`[AMP Relay] Failed to update delivery attempt for ${messageId}:`, error)  
   216→    return false  
   217→  }  
   218→}  
   219→  
   220→/**  
   221→ * Check if an agent has any non-expired pending messages  
   222→ */  
   223→export function hasPendingMessages(agentId: string): boolean {  
   224→  const dir = getAgentRelayDir(agentId)  
   225→  
   226→  if (!fs.existsSync(dir)) {  
   227→    return false  
   228→  }  
   229→  
   230→  const now = new Date()  
   231→  const files = fs.readdirSync(dir).filter(f => f.endsWith('.json'))  
   232→  
   233→  for (const file of files) {  
   234→    try {  
   235→      const content = fs.readFileSync(path.join(dir, file), 'utf-8')  
   236→      const msg = JSON.parse(content) as AMPPendingMessage  
   237→      if (new Date(msg.expires_at) >= now) {  
   238→        return true  
   239→      }  
   240→    } catch {  
   241→      // Skip invalid files  
   242→    }  
   243→  }  
   244→  
   245→  return false  
   246→}  
   247→

     9→  
    10→// POST /api/teams - Create a new team  
    11→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    12→  try {  
    13→    const body = await request.json()  
    14→    const { name, description, agentIds } = body  
    15→  
    16→    if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team name is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    18→    }  
    19→  
    20→    if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentIds must be an array' }, { status: 400 })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    const team = createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [] })  
    25→    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })  
    26→  } catch (error) {  
    27→    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)

    29→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team' },

    32→  }

     4→// GET /api/teams/[id] - Get a single team  
     5→export async function GET(

     8→) {

    13→  }

    15→}

    17→// PUT /api/teams/[id] - Update a team  
    18→export async function PUT(

    20→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    21→) {  
    22→  try {  
    23→    const { id } = await params  
    24→    const body = await request.json()

    26→  
    27→    const team = updateTeam(id, { name, description, agentIds, lastMeetingAt, instructions, lastActivityAt })  
    28→    if (!team) {  
    29→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    30→    }  
    31→  
    32→    return NextResponse.json({ team })  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to update team:', error)  
    35→    return NextResponse.json(  
    36→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to update team' },  
    37→      { status: 500 }  
    38→    )  
    39→  }  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→// DELETE /api/teams/[id] - Delete a team  
    43→export async function DELETE(  
    44→  _request: NextRequest,  
    45→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    46→) {

    48→  const deleted = deleteTeam(id)  
    49→  if (!deleted) {

    53→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:45:52]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `useTeam.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts"
}

**Result:**

     1→'use client'  
     2→  
     3→import { useState, useEffect, useCallback } from 'react'  
     4→import type { Team } from '@/types/team'  
     5→  
     6→interface UseTeamResult {  
     7→  team: Team | null  
     8→  loading: boolean  
     9→  error: string | null  
    10→  updateTeam: (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => Promise<void>  
    11→  refreshTeam: () => Promise<void>  
    12→}  
    13→  
    14→export function useTeam(teamId: string | null): UseTeamResult {  
    15→  const [team, setTeam] = useState<Team | null>(null)  
    16→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false)  
    17→  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null)  
    18→  
    19→  const fetchTeam = useCallback(async () => {  
    20→    if (!teamId) return  
    21→    try {  
    22→      const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
    23→      if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')  
    24→      const data = await res.json()  
    25→      setTeam(data.team || null)  
    26→      setError(null)  
    27→    } catch (err) {  
    28→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to fetch team')  
    29→    }  
    30→  }, [teamId])  
    31→  
    32→  // Initial fetch  
    33→  useEffect(() => {  
    34→    if (!teamId) {  
    35→      setTeam(null)  
    36→      return  
    37→    }  
    38→    setLoading(true)  
    39→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    40→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    41→  
    42→  const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => {  
    43→    if (!teamId) return

    45→    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)

     9→function formatTimeAgo(iso: string): string {  
    10→  const diff = Date.now() - new Date(iso).getTime()  
    11→  const minutes = Math.floor(diff / 60000)  
    12→  if (minutes < 1) return 'just now'  
    13→  if (minutes < 60) return `${minutes}m ago`  
    14→  const hours = Math.floor(minutes / 60)  
    15→  if (hours < 24) return `${hours}h ago`  
    16→  const days = Math.floor(hours / 24)  
    17→  return `${days}d ago`  
    18→}

    14→  const [searchQuery, setSearchQuery] = useState('')

    17→    if (!searchQuery.trim()) return agents  
    18→    const q = searchQuery.toLowerCase()  
    19→    return agents.filter(a => {  
    20→      const label = (a.label || '').toLowerCase()

    47→    return false

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { loadDocuments, createDocument } from '@/lib/document-registry'  
     3→import { getTeam } from '@/lib/team-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// GET /api/teams/[id]/documents - List all documents for a team  
     6→export async function GET(  
     7→  _request: NextRequest,  
     8→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
     9→) {  
    10→  const { id } = await params  
    11→  const team = getTeam(id)  
    12→  if (!team) {  
    13→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    14→  }  
    15→  const documents = loadDocuments(id)  
    16→  return NextResponse.json({ documents })  
    17→}  
    18→  
    19→// POST /api/teams/[id]/documents - Create a new document  
    20→export async function POST(  
    21→  request: NextRequest,  
    22→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    23→) {  
    24→  try {  
    25→    const { id } = await params  
    26→    const team = getTeam(id)  
    27→    if (!team) {  
    28→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    const body = await request.json()  
    32→    const { title, content, pinned, tags } = body  
    33→  
    34→    if (!title || typeof title !== 'string') {  
    35→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'title is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    36→    }  
    37→  
    38→    const document = createDocument({  
    39→      teamId: id,  
    40→      title,  
    41→      content: content || '',  
    42→      pinned,  
    43→      tags,  
    44→    })  
    45→  
    46→    return NextResponse.json({ document }, { status: 201 })  
    47→  } catch (error) {  
    48→    console.error('Failed to create document:', error)  
    49→    return NextResponse.json(  
    50→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create document' },  
    51→      { status: 500 }  
    52→    )  
    53→  }  
    54→}

    20	function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    21	  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {

    23	  }

    26	function pruneOldEnded(meetings: Meeting[]): Meeting[] {  
    27	  const cutoff = Date.now() - PRUNE_DAYS * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000  
    28	  return meetings.filter(m => {  
    29	    if (m.status !== 'ended' || !m.endedAt) return true  
    30	    return new Date(m.endedAt).getTime() > cutoff  
    31	  })  
    32	}  
    33	  
    34	export function loadMeetings(): Meeting[] {  
    35	  try {  
    36	    ensureTeamsDir()  
    37	    if (!fs.existsSync(MEETINGS_FILE)) {  
    38	      return []  
    39	    }  
    40	    const data = fs.readFileSync(MEETINGS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    41	    const parsed: MeetingsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    42	    const meetings = Array.isArray(parsed.meetings) ? parsed.meetings : []  
    43	    // Auto-prune old ended meetings  
    44	    const pruned = pruneOldEnded(meetings)  
    45	    if (pruned.length !== meetings.length) {  
    46	      saveMeetings(pruned)  
    47	    }  
    48	    return pruned  
    49	  } catch (error) {  
    50	    console.error('Failed to load meetings:', error)  
    51	    return []  
    52	  }  
    53	}

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 05:50:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Design a detailed implementation plan for adding Team Governance (open/closed teams with messaging isolation) to AI Maestro.  

## CONTEXT  

AI Maestro is a Next.js 14 dashboard for managing AI coding agents. It has a Team Meeting system where teams are groups of agents with kanban boards, tasks, and documents. Currently there is ZERO authentication/authorization on any API route (Phase 1 = localhost-only).  

The user wants to add messaging governance to prevent agents from different projects/teams from interfering with each other's communications and kanban boards.  

## REQUIREMENTS  

### Team Types  
- Add `type: 'open' | 'closed'` to existing Team entity  
- Open teams: current behavior (no restrictions, anyone can create/manage)  
- Closed teams: strict messaging isolation and access control  

### Roles  
- **MANAGER**: Global singleton. Can manage ALL teams, send/receive to ALL agents, belong to multiple teams.  
- **CHIEF-OF-STAFF**: Per-team leader. Can manage their team, send/receive to ALL agents in their team + other CHIEF-OF-STAFF + MANAGER. Can belong to multiple teams.  
- Only USER can assign/remove MANAGER and CHIEF-OF-STAFF roles (password-protected)  

### Messaging Rules (Closed Teams)  
- Normal agents: can ONLY send/receive within their own closed team  
- CHIEF-OF-STAFF: can send/receive within their team + cross-team to other CHIEF-OF-STAFF and MANAGER  
- MANAGER: can send/receive to anyone  
- Open teams: no messaging restrictions (current behavior preserved)  

### Team Management Rules (Closed Teams)  
- Only MANAGER and CHIEF-OF-STAFF can create/delete closed teams  
- Only MANAGER and CHIEF-OF-STAFF can assign/unassign/transfer agents  
- When agent is assigned to a closed team, auto-removed from any previous closed team (forced transfer)  
- Normal agents can be in at most ONE closed team (can be in many open teams)  

### Kanban/Task ACL (Closed Teams)  
- Only team members, CHIEF-OF-STAFF, and MANAGER can see/modify tasks for closed teams  
- Only team members, CHIEF-OF-STAFF, and MANAGER can see/modify documents for closed teams  

### Password System  
- User sets a governance password (never stored, only bcrypt hash kept)  
- Required when assigning/removing MANAGER or CHIEF-OF-STAFF roles  
- Phase 2: Password recovery via OS-native notifications (macOS: osascript, Linux: notify-send)  

## EXISTING ARCHITECTURE (from exploration)  

### Types to Modify:  
- `types/team.ts`: Team interface (lines 8-18) - needs type, chiefOfStaffId, governance fields  
- `types/agent.ts`: Agent interface (lines 152-228) - team field is free-text string, needs to reference Team.id  

### Storage:  
- Teams: `~/.aimaestro/teams/teams.json` (lib/team-registry.ts)  
- Tasks: `~/.aimaestro/teams/tasks-{teamId}.json` (lib/task-registry.ts)  
- Documents: `~/.aimaestro/teams/docs-{teamId}.json` (lib/document-registry.ts)  
- Agents: `~/.aimaestro/agents/registry.json` (lib/agent-registry.ts)  
- New governance config will need a home  

### API Routes to Add ACL:  
- `app/api/teams/route.ts` - POST (create team)  

... [2410 more chars truncated]  

</div>

     1→/**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Registry - File-based CRUD for team persistence  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/teams.json  
     5→ * Mirrors the pattern from lib/agent-registry.ts  
     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→import fs from 'fs'  
     9→import path from 'path'  
    10→import os from 'os'  
    11→import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'  
    12→import type { Team, TeamsFile } from '@/types/team'  
    13→  
    14→const AIMAESTRO_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')  
    15→const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'teams')  
    16→const TEAMS_FILE = path.join(TEAMS_DIR, 'teams.json')  
    17→  
    18→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    19→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    20→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    21→  }  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
    25→  try {  
    26→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    27→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
    28→      return []  
    29→    }  
    30→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    31→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    32→    return Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→export function saveTeams(teams: Team[]): boolean {  
    40→  try {  
    41→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    42→    const file: TeamsFile = { version: 1, teams }  
    43→    fs.writeFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    44→    return true  
    45→  } catch (error) {  
    46→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
    47→    return false  
    48→  }  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→export function getTeam(id: string): Team | null {  
    52→  const teams = loadTeams()  
    53→  return teams.find(t => t.id === id) || null  
    54→}  
    55→  
    56→export function createTeam(data: { name: string; description?: string; agentIds: string[] }): Team {  
    57→  const teams = loadTeams()  
    58→  const now = new Date().toISOString()  
    59→

    23→function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {

    26→  
    27→export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {  
    28→  try {  
    29→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    30→    const filePath = tasksFilePath(teamId)  
    31→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    32→      return []  
    33→    }  
    34→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    35→    const parsed: TasksFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    36→    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
    37→  } catch (error) {  
    38→    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    39→    return []  
    40→  }  
    41→}  
    42→  
    43→export function saveTasks(teamId: string, tasks: Task[]): boolean {  
    44→  try {  
    45→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    46→    const file: TasksFile = { version: 1, tasks }  
    47→    fs.writeFileSync(tasksFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    48→    return true  
    49→  } catch (error) {  
    50→    console.error(`Failed to save tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    51→    return false  
    52→  }  
    53→}

    11→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    12→  try {  
    13→    const body = await request.json()  
    14→    const { name, description, agentIds } = body  
    15→  
    16→    if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team name is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    18→    }  
    19→  
    20→    if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentIds must be an array' }, { status: 400 })  
    22→    }  
    23→

    25→    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })

     1→/**  
     2→ * AMP v1 Route Endpoint  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue  
    28→ */

**Result:**

    60→  
    61→/** Rate limit: max requests per agent per window */  
    62→const RATE_LIMIT_MAX = 60  
    63→const RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MS = 60_000  
    64→  
    65→// ============================================================================  
    66→// Rate Limiter (in-memory, per-agent)  
    67→// ============================================================================  
    68→  
    69→const rateLimitMap = new Map<string, { count: number; resetAt: number }>()  
    70→  
    71→interface RateLimitResult {  
    72→  allowed: boolean  
    73→  limit: number  
    74→  remaining: number  
    75→  resetAt: number  
    76→}  
    77→  
    78→function checkRateLimit(agentId: string): RateLimitResult {  
    79→  const now = Date.now()  
    80→  const entry = rateLimitMap.get(agentId)  
    81→  
    82→  if (!entry || now > entry.resetAt) {  
    83→    rateLimitMap.set(agentId, { count: 1, resetAt: now + RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MS })  
    84→    return { allowed: true, limit: RATE_LIMIT_MAX, remaining: RATE_LIMIT_MAX - 1, resetAt: now + RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MS }  
    85→  }  
    86→  
    87→  if (entry.count >= RATE_LIMIT_MAX) {  
    88→    return { allowed: false, limit: RATE_LIMIT_MAX, remaining: 0, resetAt: entry.resetAt }  
    89→  }  
    90→  
    91→  entry.count++  
    92→  // Periodic cleanup: remove expired entries every 100 checks  
    93→  if (entry.count % 100 === 0) {  
    94→    for (const [key, val] of rateLimitMap) {  
    95→      if (now > val.resetAt) rateLimitMap.delete(key)  
    96→    }  
    97→  }  
    98→  return { allowed: true, limit: RATE_LIMIT_MAX, remaining: RATE_LIMIT_MAX - entry.count, resetAt: entry.resetAt }  
    99→}  
   100→  
   101→// ============================================================================  
   102→// Helpers  
   103→// ============================================================================

   106→ * Parse an AMP address into components.

   108→ * Address format: name@[scope.]tenant.provider  
   109→ * Examples:  
   110→ *   alice@rnd23bl  

... [6239 more chars truncated]

    60→  
    61→/**  
    62→ * Get this host's name for messages  
    63→ */  
    64→function getHostName(): string {  
    65→  try {  
    66→    const selfHost = getSelfHost()  
    67→    return selfHost.name || getSelfHostId() || 'unknown-host'

    73→/**  
    74→ * Build AMP envelope + payload from web UI message params  
    75→ */  
    76→function buildAMPEnvelope(message: Message): { envelope: AMPEnvelope; payload: AMPPayload } {  
    77→  const selfHostId = getSelfHostId() || getHostName()  
    78→  const msgIdNormalized = message.id.replace(/-/g, '_')  
    79→  const envelope: AMPEnvelope = {  
    80→    version: 'amp/0.1',  
    81→    id: msgIdNormalized,  
    82→    from: `${message.fromAlias || message.from}@${selfHostId}.aimaestro.local`,  
    83→    to: `${message.toAlias || message.to}@${(message.toHost || selfHostId)}.aimaestro.local`,  
    84→    subject: message.subject,  
    85→    priority: message.priority,  
    86→    timestamp: message.timestamp,  
    87→    signature: message.amp?.signature || '',  
    88→    thread_id: message.inReplyTo || msgIdNormalized,  
    89→  }  
    90→  if (message.inReplyTo) {  
    91→    envelope.in_reply_to = message.inReplyTo  
    92→  }  
    93→  const payload: AMPPayload = {  
    94→    type: message.content.type,  
    95→    message: message.content.message,  
    96→    context: message.content.context,  
    97→  }  
    98→  return { envelope, payload }  
    99→}

    23→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, `docs-${teamId}.json`)  
    24→}  
    25→  
    26→export function loadDocuments(teamId: string): TeamDocument[] {  
    27→  try {  
    28→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    29→    const filePath = docsFilePath(teamId)  
    30→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    31→      return []  
    32→    }  
    33→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    34→    const parsed: TeamDocumentsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    35→    return Array.isArray(parsed.documents) ? parsed.documents : []  
    36→  } catch (error) {  
    37→    console.error(`Failed to load documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    38→    return []  
    39→  }  
    40→}  
    41→  
    42→export function saveDocuments(teamId: string, documents: TeamDocument[]): boolean {  
    43→  try {  
    44→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    45→    const file: TeamDocumentsFile = { version: 1, documents }  
    46→    fs.writeFileSync(docsFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    47→    return true  
    48→  } catch (error) {  
    49→    console.error(`Failed to save documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    50→    return false  
    51→  }  
    52→}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team types for the Team Meeting feature  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Teams represent groups of agents that can be assembled into  
     5→ * a "war room" for multi-agent coordination sessions.  
     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→export interface Team {  
     9→  id: string              // UUID

    18→function ensureTeamsDir() {

    23→  
    24→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
    25→  try {  
    26→    ensureTeamsDir()

    28→      return []  
    29→    }  
    30→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')

    32→    return Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→

    44→    return true  
    45→  } catch (error) {  
    46→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
    47→    return false  
    48→  }  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→export function getTeam(id: string): Team | null {

    54→}

   458→/**  
   459→ * Update an agent  
   460→ */  
   461→export function updateAgent(id: string, updates: UpdateAgentRequest): Agent | null {  
   462→  const agents = loadAgents()  
   463→  const index = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === id)  
   464→  
   465→  if (index === -1) {  
   466→    return null  
   467→  }  
   468→  
   469→  // Support both new 'name' and deprecated 'alias'  
   470→  // Normalize to lowercase for case-insensitive consistency  
   471→  const newName = (updates.name || updates.alias)?.toLowerCase()  
   472→  const currentName = agents[index].name || agents[index].alias  
   473→  const agentHostId = agents[index].hostId || getSelfHostId()  
   474→  
   475→  // Check name uniqueness ON THIS HOST if being updated  
   476→  if (newName && newName.toLowerCase() !== currentName?.toLowerCase()) {  
   477→    const existing = getAgentByName(newName, agentHostId)  
   478→    if (existing && existing.id !== id) {  
   479→      throw new Error(`Agent "${newName}" already exists on host "${agentHostId}"`)

# Team Governance Implementation Plan for AI Maestro  

## Executive Summary  

This plan adds team governance (open/closed teams with messaging isolation) to AI Maestro. The feature introduces role-based access control (MANAGER, CHIEF-OF-STAFF) for closed teams, messaging filtering, and ACL enforcement on team resources (tasks, documents). Open teams retain current behavior with zero breaking changes.  

---  

## 1. Type Definitions (New & Modified)  

### 1.1 Modified: `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/team.ts`  

Add governance fields to the `Team` interface:  

```typescript
// New types to add at top of file
export type TeamType = 'open' | 'closed'
export type GovernanceRole = 'MANAGER' | 'CHIEF-OF-STAFF'

// Modified Team interface - add these fields after line 17 (lastActivityAt):
export interface Team {
  id: string
  name: string
  description?: string
  agentIds: string[]
  instructions?: string
  createdAt: string
  updatedAt: string
  lastMeetingAt?: string
  lastActivityAt?: string
  // NEW GOVERNANCE FIELDS:
  type: TeamType                    // 'open' (default) or 'closed'
  chiefOfStaffId?: string           // Agent UUID designated as COS for this team
}
```

### 1.2 New File: `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/governance.ts`  

```typescript
export type GovernanceRole = 'MANAGER' | 'CHIEF-OF-STAFF'

/** Stored in ~/.aimaestro/governance.json */
export interface GovernanceConfig {
  version: 1
  /** bcrypt hash of the governance password (set by user) */
  passwordHash: string | null
  /** Agent UUID of the singleton MANAGER (only one at a time) */
  managerId: string | null
  /** ISO timestamp of when password was last set */
  passwordSetAt: string | null
}
```

### 1.3 Modified: `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/agent.ts`  

The `team?: string` field on line 187 is currently a free-text string. It will NOT be changed to a Team.id reference in Phase 1 -- instead, the governance system uses `Team.agentIds` and `Team.chiefOfStaffId` as the source of truth for membership. The agent's `team` field remains a display-only label.  

No changes to `types/agent.ts` are needed.
